<name>Rodney S<//name><Date>1467145845096</Date><Rating>4</Rating>< text>
Zetton on it!  Zetton on it!

Ramen Zetton, the popular Costa Mesa ramen shop, has a new branch nearby me in Cypress.  For their soft opening, Ramen Zetton has priced their ramen bowls from $5 - $7.  Being a ramen lover & not one to pass up a discount, I hurried down to Ramen Zetton, eagerly awaiting slurping up some piping hot ramen.

The traditional ramen condiments are well represented - chili oil, white pepper grinder, vinegar, red chili pepper & house made spicy miso chili paste.

The house made spicy miso chili paste has a definite kick to it.  Not for spice weaklings.

I went for their signature Sesame Miso Tantan ramen ($7, reg. price $8.50)-

The tantan ramen broth is thick, almost curry-like.  Adding the entire jar of spicy miso chili paste, the broth became almost akin to marinara.  Plus, a splash of vinegar, some chili pepper, a drizzling of chili oil, freshly ground white pepper & a splash or 2 of vinegar. The vinegar is what really kicked the flavor profile up a notch.   Hearty & rich, the sesame miso tantan consisted of a special blend of sesame & miso, chicken broth, green onion, ground pork & vegetable puree.  The ramen had a good bite to it.  My preference would've enjoyed them more al dente, but I was not disappointed with the wonderfully thick broth & juicy chunks of ground pork.  At $7, a delicious bowl that's a must get!

Not feeling soup today?  Ramen Zetton's simplistic menu also has various rice dishes & gyoza for your consideration.

Service was good.  I arrived a few minutes before opening.  The father of the owner of Ramen Zetton was running the place.  The cook called in sick & one from the Costa Mesa location was brought in to save the day.  My water was refilled on a couple occasions & I was even given containers of the spicy miso chili paste to take home, w/o asking.  Not a place for large groups, seating is minimal with a few tables, booths & bar seating.

Parking is in private lot.  Hard to spot from the street, Ramen Zetton is located behind Oodles of Noodles Pho Restaurant & adjacent to Poki Roll.

Hurry & get down to Zetton!  Ramen Zetton serves up soothing bowls of ramen that are priced cheaper than their competitors.  The sesame miso tantan ramen was a winner & I'm eagerly anticipating trying their other ramen offerings.  I can't procrastinate, though, as I want to take advantage of Ramen Zetton's soft opening pricing.  Hungry for soup? Check out Ramen Zetton!

Highly recommend!
NOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOMNOM</text>

Lots of parking in the lot, near by Icon (For you craft beer people)

The noodles for the $5 are thinner (Chuka-Soba), while the Ramen for the $6 are thicker. Service here with one person is pretty awesome I have to say, even with a packed house.

< Review>
Lovely little coffee shop for the hipster crowd.  They literally serve avocado toast here and it tastes amazing.  Their coffee is made well and there is a great variety of cold brews to choose from.  The decor in the cafe is very trendy and there are outlets at most of the tables so that you can plug in your laptop and complete the vibe of this cafe.  Service was friendly and we had a great experience here.  Will definitely be back.</Review>

<review>This is such a unique vibe and a nice low key place to relax, either on your own or with a couple of friends, or focus and get some quality work or study done. There is usually plenty of seating options depending on what you're looking for. One of my favorite spots for really good avocado toast and lots of variety when it comes to selection of drinks. I've been a few times and the menu changes up slightly which is nice to keep the food options fresh and add some variety. Although the location has more a of an industrial feel to it than the typical plaza or strip mall, it‚Äôs easy to find by following google maps and there is plenty of parking options. They have a play area and activities for parents who want to relax while spending some time with their kids and the clientele that comes here seems to be cognizant of not making too much noise. Service is always great! They‚Äôre polite and helpful with any questions. Service is pretty quick considering everything is made from scratch. If you want a coffee shop with a bit of a twist and a menu that‚Äôs not like the brand names, highly recommend you try the Dirty Penguin.<//review>< UserId.>

< Review>
Eagle Mine is not only a fun and interesting place to learn about California History, the people running it  couldn‚Äôt have been nicer!  We visited yesterday with my 93-year-old Mother.  We were greeted with friendly smiles and treated like honored guests.  One staff member even offered to stay up-top and visit with my mom while my husband and I toured the mine. We didn‚Äôt take her up on this, as we have been down the mine before and on this visit just chose to wander around the property and look at all the cool antique mining and farming equipment.  We also enjoyed the gift shop with its collection of unique jewelry, books and doo-dads.  As we left, I felt badly as I realized that we hadn‚Äôt actually given the place any business even though they graciously allowed us the use of their very clean restrooms, carried a chair across the grounds specifically for my mom to sit on, took several pictures of us and repeatedly checked to see if we needed any help.  I hope that letting everyone know about this wonderful place and its lovely staff, helps make up for that by bringing The Eagle Mine more visitors.  We will definitely be back and will bring kids, grandkids and friends to experience this tiny step back into California History.  Thank you Eagle Mine for your kindness.
PS ‚Äì I don‚Äôt think I left a review from three years ago when my husband and I toured the mine, but that was a great experience as well.  I highly recommend it!< /Review>

['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPAZS5IXxdnJ-BAUntfIBxkqY9atdoTTJdB2_0G=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPMNc5AzIe0Kj8165B4NT8G8n6PYSMoPvY5f3Gl=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOFWc7fThHDzu447ILuIgC9Ca3eXZiohGqWeo51=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//pics>< text>
A MUST SEE!  2017 marks the 50th anniversary of the Eagle & High Peak Mines, the mother lode of SoCal. Lovingly preserved by Craig & Paul Nelson, the grandsons of the original miner, for its educational and historic value since 1967. Bargain day trip!!! $10 admission has remained the same for three decades. CASH ONLY.  Professional guided tours, led by a real miner and prospector. Our guide, Matthew, a credentialed geologist whose immense knowledge of geology, Julian's gold mining history, underground operation, and milling process, made a very interesting and .  Tour 1000 feet of underground, hard rock tunnel, and relive the history of the 1870 mine amidst the authentic tools and machinery used.  Steep stairs inside the mine, more than half-way through, so I had to walk back with my real service dog, but the tour was complete enough for me.  My husband continued on and was impressed!  See gold bearing quartz veins, antique vehicles, tools, implements and a huge rock and mineral museum.  Big gift shop in the barn, great for rock hound enthusiasts and beginning collectors. Simulated boot hill. Shaded, pleasant picnic area. Gold panning facilities (gold is recycled for the next visitors, so you can't keep it,) and quick how-to demos. Only six blocks off Julian's Main Street, you can drive or walk in.  Plenty of pea gravel parking, buses okay.  Special arrangements made for geology students (groups), colleges, schools, and film industry.  Clean restrooms. Real (professionally trained) service animals only, allowed inside the mine.  I look forward to my return (loaded picnic basket in tow), to bring my adult kids and grandson for a day of family fun.</text>

<GmapID>0x80dbd00e112e4949:0x9efeaa4112383d0d<//GmapID><UserId.>113107298903632484509<//UserId.>< text>
So we go up to pick apples in Julian like all the other 50,000 people this weekend and realize all the orchards are closed for u-pick. So we go into a little orchard market named Wynola Flats owned by Mike, our new friend, who tells us to check out this Eagle Mining Company.  I'm thinking "This guy Mike knows a lot about apples, and about honey, so yeah, we'll give him a shot on his gold mine recommendation".  So we drive there, bypassing the hordes of people waiting in line for pies in downtown Julian.  First thing we notice when we get out of the car was the owner inside of the shop waves us in and asks us if we want to go on the tour. Of course we do. So we sign up. Cheap, only $10 each. You can spend more on a Kombucha in Los Angeles for this price. We start our tour and our guide starts taking us on a mystical journey into the realm of 1870s hard-rock gold mining. We learn about the rock crusher, the separation process, and he takes us into the gold mine. This is not your grand-pappys ten cent gold mine. It's the real deal. We got deep into this thing, all the while at each bend learning something new about how these hard-core miner guys mined for gold back in the day. At the end, we even got to pan for gold. REAL GOLD. So I'm acquiring a new hobby and adding "Gold-Panning Pan" on my Christmas list. I learned more in this one-hour tour than my entire elementary school education. Maybe high school as well. And it was only ten dollars. Consider what you can do with ten dollars. Forego that next Kombucha, skip the pie lines in Julian, and head to the Eagle Mining Company. You'll be glad you did!<//text>

104750879713406235231</user_id>
< Text>
This is a great spot. The owners do a lot to make this work.  I will say, it has changed more recently.  I'm not sure why the museum area has been neglected as it is.  In fact, the word neglect doesn't even go far enough.  They seem to use it as a giant scrap closet now- absolute shame in my opinion.  Visitors have no idea what they are missing out on.  They do not know that their tour has had 15-20 minutes shaved off the original tour.

If you stop in, look to meet Craig.   This man pours his heart and soul into this business.  For him, I doubt he sees a business. I'm sure he sees much more.  I say this because noone would work as hard as he does just for some money.  When I mentioned that I was surprised that the mines weren't dustier, he told us that he walks down the tunnels every day before the tours with buckets of water.  The water helps to hold the dust down.  Now, this man is pushing 50 and stood before us with a cast on his foot.  He had recently broken it.  But his dedication does not allow him to stop. He is dedicated to creating an experience.   He is dedicated to keeping this place alive.  This dedication is something I very much respect.

One last thing, I see others saying they only take cash for the tour.  That is simply not true.  They take cash,PayPal, or check for the tour.  For items in the shop, I believe they will only accept cash.</Text>

< Review>
This place was the high point of our visit to Julian. I thought it would be the most touristy place, but it turned out to be the least touristy place. The tour is actually of two mines that were run from the 1870s until the depression. Our tour guide was tremendously knowledgeable and oddly passionate about mining. He taught us a lot of things, from the history of this particular place and how it led to Julian‚Äôs growth, to the actual mechanics and economics of mining.

We were truly impressed. Plus, it was fun! There was just enough walking to burn some of those calories from eating apple pie and drinking apple cider, but not enough to deter older visitors or people who don‚Äôt like walking (although there is one narrow and steep passage that might be tough for older folks).<//Review>

< text>
To be honest, I wasn't sure what to expect, but my wife and I really did enjoy our tour this past weekend. The guide was informative, and the entire experience was surprisingly educational.

Only thing I'd "warn" about, is that this is a REAL mine, and isn't terribly comfortable for a tall person to move-around in. You can wack your head pretty easily if you're not careful, and hiking-out the last (fairly long) stretch while hunched-over wasn't comfortable.

Still, I'm glad that they left the tunnels alone, rather than modifying them for tourism. It made the experience all that more authentic!</text>

<user_name>K Mulcahy</user_name><user>103632557579135783842< /user><gmapID>0x80dc735d0201b405:0xa09006a20b74a3d0< /gmapID><Pics>None</Pics><date>1554436153147</date><Response>None</Response><rate>4<//rate>< Text>
First time eating there today and I'll be back if I'm nearby.  I had homemade fettuccine with porcini mushrooms, a special today.  It was good but seriously under-salted.  After correcting that, I really enjoyed the dish.  The mushrooms were especially tasty.  I wish they had side salads since it's a huge amount of undiluted carbs.  Maybe make the pasta portions a bit smaller and include a little salad?  I saw about half the patrons having entree salads which looked very nice but they were too large for a side dish.  Beyond that, it's all self-serve, very clean, minimal and functional.  Huge amount of space between tables so all is calm and serenity.  Final plus is the friendliness and patience of the staff.  Good feelings here.</Text>
